<div id="review_238069280" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238069280" />
    <a title="Jam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2740288-jam"><img alt="Jam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320844683p2/2740288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238069280?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jam" href="/user/show/2740288-jam">Jam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2740288-jam?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238069280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer147130987526097094">The book is well-written, and some parts are actually enjoyable, but I only gave it one star because half of the book focused on a character which I found to be absolutely irritating. Halfway into it, I was prepared to throw it away. I found the character to be that annoying. But, I didn't throw it away. Instead, I skipped all the way to the end, and found out that this character, Terisa Morgan, doesn't get any better. She stays almost as weak and stupid as she was at the start of the novel, onl</span>
  <span id="freeText147130987526097094" style="display:none">The book is well-written, and some parts are actually enjoyable, but I only gave it one star because half of the book focused on a character which I found to be absolutely irritating. Halfway into it, I was prepared to throw it away. I found the character to be that annoying. But, I didn't throw it away. Instead, I skipped all the way to the end, and found out that this character, Terisa Morgan, doesn't get any better. She stays almost as weak and stupid as she was at the start of the novel, only mildly showing some intelligence at the very very very end of the book. For a person who likes strong women characters, or at least female characters who may start out weak, but who at least emerge stronger a lot earlier in the the book, I really really hated this character. She didn't think. She kept getting fooled by the same man. She was constantly weak and needed to be defended. No doubt, she had a worthwhile part to play as the other "hero" of the story, but it was overshadowed by the constant barrage of insults piling up in my head.<br /><br />I'm going to read the second novel, but only because I want to know what happens to Geraden. He may be foolish and clumsy, but at least he has a brain. </span>
  <a data-text-id="147130987526097094" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/456306853?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabina" href="/user/show/8815741-sabina">Sabina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer456306853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7152563003798725903">It's been a while since I read this book. Stephen Donaldson has a way of creating thoroughly dislikeable lead characters. I found the same with his Thomas Covenant series, where I was getting increasingly annoyed with Thomas' whining and poor action. This book is much the same in that regard as Terisa's self-involved ignorance gave me, to put it crudely, the shits. There were so many instances in which even a young child would have thought 'hang on a sec, this doesn't seem right' and yet she is </span>
  <span id="freeText7152563003798725903" style="display:none">It's been a while since I read this book. Stephen Donaldson has a way of creating thoroughly dislikeable lead characters. I found the same with his Thomas Covenant series, where I was getting increasingly annoyed with Thomas' whining and poor action. This book is much the same in that regard as Terisa's self-involved ignorance gave me, to put it crudely, the shits. There were so many instances in which even a young child would have thought 'hang on a sec, this doesn't seem right' and yet she is completely unaware.<br />I understand that Donaldson's aim was perhaps to have his readers witness the growth of a woman, to have her come into her own and become, well, real. But I find that concept itself quite difficult to deal with, the idea that women ought to undergo trauma and sexual objectification and abuse in order to grow. Unlike her male counterpart, Terisa's main purpose was to have things happen TO her. <br />The fantasy world was interesting, though, as was the way in which magic functioned. And, though I spent a good amount of the first book just wishing Terisa dead so that we could actually concentrate on the story and on Gerarden without her incessant idiocy getting in the way, I did want to continue reading it and read the concluding book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7152563003798725903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3215042695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3215042695" />
    <a title="Jen526" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2230469-jen526"><img alt="Jen526" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3215042695?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen526" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen526" href="/user/show/2230469-jen526">Jen526</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2230469-jen526?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3215042695&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3215042695" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6909097959025735232">Definitely not a book for those who lean toward faster pacing or action. This book is almost entirely palace intrigue, with the characters mostly just having lots of questions, with most true answers put off until the next volume. I enjoyed it a lot as a bit of a different sort of take on both a portal fantasy and a coming of age story. Our heroine is someone who is pulled into another world to be a "savior", but has no real skills to bring to the table and has to immediately contend with multip</span>
  <span id="freeText6909097959025735232" style="display:none">Definitely not a book for those who lean toward faster pacing or action. This book is almost entirely palace intrigue, with the characters mostly just having lots of questions, with most true answers put off until the next volume. I enjoyed it a lot as a bit of a different sort of take on both a portal fantasy and a coming of age story. Our heroine is someone who is pulled into another world to be a "savior", but has no real skills to bring to the table and has to immediately contend with multiple factions wanting to use her for their own aims - some of whom believe she's the savior, some who think she's an enemy, and others who dismiss her as a mistake and waste of time. Add to this that she, herself, is emotionally damaged without an ounce of personal self-esteem, and the story mostly becomes about Teresa moving from a passive non-entity going down a path of least resistance to someone who pushes past her perceptions of her own limitations and tries to pursue what she thinks is the right course of action as much as she can. I tend to be a fan of books where the story is as much about the characters working through their own inner demons as it is about the external save-the-world plot, and this book is a fairly textbook example of that sort of approach.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6909097959025735232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6552287055096913703">I really enjoyed the feel the prologue gave to the whole book. Several of the characters were week and frustrating, but the teased curse in the prologue made it excusable.<br/>This was a book club book and I didn't do my due diligence to realize before the last 20 pages this was a duology, which gave out a very sudden and unsatisfying ending. <br/>After I read the 2nd book I may come back a chance my star rating. Up if it wraps up many of the mysteries the 1st book has me invested in our down if it doesn'</span>
  <span id="freeText6552287055096913703" style="display:none">I really enjoyed the feel the prologue gave to the whole book. Several of the characters were week and frustrating, but the teased curse in the prologue made it excusable.<br />This was a book club book and I didn't do my due diligence to realize before the last 20 pages this was a duology, which gave out a very sudden and unsatisfying ending. <br />After I read the 2nd book I may come back a chance my star rating. Up if it wraps up many of the mysteries the 1st book has me invested in our down if it doesn't pay off I the end. Stay tuned...<br /><br />Final verdict: Not everything paid off as much as I would have liked, but still comfortable leaving this at 3 stars.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('acfx7AYomfXV0snKW5/FwyymV2wdkJi5pc00LsSfV1sNcgqtvieT69gco8EOhz1NSkGZT08QR2SUvhP5k0MLgA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yA4qxWvwVIMnnNgog/fCn9tLUvjK5ea4MsSvE5ikRLWsu9GE0/9enSpSsiPW7zoRvayc25hlOWUDt4jEz3gYbg==')})
  }

A losing game of chance with a mysterious stranger seems like a dream to young King Tamar, but the iron ring on his finger is a very real token that his life may be forfeit. A journey to the stranger\'s distant kingdom seems his only chance to discover the truth. Many adventures and diversions crop up along the way as Tamar gains some surprising companions, including a brave and beautiful milkmaid, a cowardly eagle, and a wiley monkey king who used to be a man. The author\'s flexible style moves smoothly from comedy to tragedy and back again; from battle scenes to ridiculous situations, Alexander never loses the thread. Set within the action are small gems of poetry and folktales. The concept of dharma, or proper conduct, and the rigid caste system deeply affect Tamar\'s actions. Plot, characters, and setting all have their parts to play, but it is the tension set up among the lively characters and the cultural conventions binding them that create the structure of the story and lead inevitably to its conclusion.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/12980.Stephen_R_Donaldson">About Stephen R. Donaldson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/12980.Stephen_R_Donaldson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1425823085p3/12980.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10893936957385666468">Stephen Reeder Donaldson is an American fantasy, science fiction, and mystery novelist; in the United Kingdom he is usually called "Stephen Donaldson" (without the "R"). He has also written non-fiction under the pen name Reed Stephens.<br/><br/>EARLY LIFE AND EDUCATION:<br/><br/>Stephen R. Donaldson was born May 13, 1947 in Cleveland, Ohio. His father, James, was a medical missionary and his mother, Ruth, a prostheti</span>
  <span id="freeText10893936957385666468" style="display:none">Stephen Reeder Donaldson is an American fantasy, science fiction, and mystery novelist; in the United Kingdom he is usually called "Stephen Donaldson" (without the "R"). He has also written non-fiction under the pen name Reed Stephens.<br /><br />EARLY LIFE AND EDUCATION:<br /><br />Stephen R. Donaldson was born May 13, 1947 in Cleveland, Ohio. His father, James, was a medical missionary and his mother, Ruth, a prosthetist (a person skilled in making or fitting prosthetic devices). Donaldson spent the years between the ages of 3 and 16 living in India, where his father was working as an orthopaedic surgeon. Donaldson earned his bachelor's degree from The College of Wooster and master's degree from Kent State University. <br /><br />INSPIRATIONS:<br /><br />Donaldson's work is heavily influenced by other fantasy authors such as J.R.R. Tolkien, Roger Zelazny, Joseph Conrad, Henry James, and William Faulkner. The writers he most admires are Patricia A. McKillip, Steven Erikson, and Tim Powers.<br /><br />It is believed that a speech his father made on leprosy (whilst working with lepers in India) led to Donaldson's creation of Thomas Covenant, the anti-hero of his most famous work (Thomas Covenant). The first book in that series, <i>Lord Foul's Bane</i>, received 47 rejections before a publisher agreed to publish it.<br /><br />PROMINENT WORK:<br />Stephen Donaldson came to prominence in 1977 with the The Chronicles of Thomas Covenant, which is centred around a leper shunned by society and his trials and tribulations as his destiny unfolds. These books established Donaldson as one of the most important figures in modern fantasy fiction.<br /><br />PERSONAL LIFE:<br />He currently resides in New Mexico.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.stephendonaldson.com/fromtheauthor/gi.php" rel="nofollow noopener">THE GRADUAL INTERVIEW</a><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10893936957385666468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;The story of Terisa and Geraden began very much like a fable. She was a princess in a high tower. He was a hero come to rescue her. She was the only daughter of wealth and power. He was the seventh son of the lord of the seventh Care. She was beautiful from the auburn hair that crowned her head to the tips of her white toes. He was handsome and courageous. She was held prisoner by enchantment. He was a fearless breaker of enchantments.<br /><br />As in all the fables, they were made for each other.&rdquo;</span>
